produce by sue asscher journal of australian exploration by augustus charle gregory cmg frg etc gold medalist royal geographical society and franci thoma gregory frg etc etc gold medalist royal geographical society brisbane : jame c beal government printer william street 1884 preface numerous inquiry have be make for copy of the journal of the exploration by the messr gregory in the western northern and central portion of australium and as these journal have hitherto only be partially publish in a fragmentary form and be now out of print it have be deem desirable to collect the material into one volume for convenience of reference and to place on permanent record some of the earlier attempt to penetrate the terra incognita which then constitute so vast a portion of the australian continent although during the twenty-two year which have elapse since the last of these expedition be undertake the geographical knowledge of australium have so far advance as to fill in most of the detail of its physical feature and set at rest the speculative opinion and theory of early explorer it have not be deem desirable to alter or amend the impression or view record at the time but simply reproduce the journal as originally compile -lrb- table of contents messr gregory 's expedition to the east and north of swan river 1846 the settler ' expedition to the northward from perth under mr 1846 early condition of west australium the colony of western australium be establish in 1829 but its isolation from the older settlement of new south wale render it necessary to import all the horse cattle and sheep by sailing vessel from tasmanium or other remote source while the heavy loss and difficulty attend long sea voyage prevent any large importation of stock -- so that though there be a fair rate of increase the flock and herd of the settler have find sufficient pasturage for the first ten year on the bank of the swan river and its upper valley the avon together with the coast district southward to the vasse inlet but after 1840 the stock-owner begin to feel that all prospect of material increase must be relinquish unless additional pasture could be discover several public as well as private expedition be undertake for the purpose of ascertain whether in the interior or along the coast on either side of the settlement there exist any available country but they have only encounter dense scrub of acacia and eucalyptus with salt marsh and scarcity of fresh water in the interior the coast to the east have be traverse from adelaide to king george 's sound by mr eyre and find to be altogether unfit for settlement while to the north the coast present a series of sandy plain for more than 200 mile it may now appear extraordinary that the earlier explorer in australium be so frequently unsuccessful in they endeavor to penetrate the interior but the scarcity of suitable horse the unsuitable character of the saddlery cumbersome camp equipment and deficiency of knowledge regard the season in the interior all combine to defeat the first explorer in district which have since be traverse with comparative facility in 1846 the known country have become so nearly stock to the full extent of its capability that the lead question of interest with the settler be where new run could be discover and among many other the messr gregory propose to attempt the further exploration of the interior messr ac and ft gregory who be attach to the department of the surveyor-general apply for three month ' leave of absence for the purpose but it be eventually arrange that the expedition should be under the auspices of the government which provide four horse and vote 5 pound for the purchase of equipment the remainder be supply at private expense the party consist of ac gregory ft gregory and hc gregory provide with four horse and seven week ' provision the equipment be reduce to the least possible weight the start point be mr tn yule 's station in the toodyay district sixty mile north-east from perth the follow be a transcript of the journal : -- exploration to east of swan river 1846 diary 7th August 1846 leave mr yule 's farm at boyeen spring pass thin ice after reach the ground which be dry enough to bear the weight of the horse we have to travel about three mile through soft dust of white gypsum in which we sink from one to two foot but at expedition and its object colonial secretary 's office perth August 28 1848 sir i be direct by the governor to inform you that you have be appoint to direct the explore expedition about to proceed northwards on account of the zeal energy and enterprising spirit that have be exhibit by you on other occasion and call into action with credit to yourself and advantage to the public interest the party under you direction it be intend should proceed northward as high as the gascoyne river -lrb- the gascoyne river flow into shark bay in latitude 24 degree 52 minute south -rrb- it be advisable to approach that river from the eastward about 100 mile from the coast after proceed in a north-easterly and northerly direction from the country abreast of champion bay it be desirable that part of you route which lie farthest in the interior country should be first accomplish in order to avail yourself of the best chance of finding water you will examine that river as far as it may be practicable to do with the view of trace its course of ascertain if possible the nature of the bar at the mouth of it and the question of its be practicable for boat to what distance from the bar and the nature of the soil in the vicinity of either bank after have examine thus the gascoyne river you will proceed in a southerly direction and examine the river as yet unnamed about forty mile farther south that flow into shark 's bay the mouth of which be see by captain gray and be place by he at point long should you proceed along the sea-shore for any distance you will pay as much attention as you limited means will allow you to do to the peculiarity of the coast and of any estuary creek or roadstead that may present themselves you will bear in mind that the primary object of this expedition be the examination of a new tract of unknown country for practical purpose by practical man -- that in fact the discovery of new land of a available kind for pasture have become a thing to be desire of paramount importance and a object in the attainment of which the interest and perhaps the fate of this colony depend you will thus conduct you expedition with the view of promote this principal object to the best of you ability but it be hardly needful to observe to you that this chief object may be promote and attain without neglect to observe the geographical geological and mineralogical feature of the country you pass through its production -- animal and vegetable and the character dialect and custom to some extent of the aboriginal tribe you may fall in with you have be so frequently employ in explore expedition though of minor importance perhaps to the present that you must be well aware it be no less impolitic than cruel to come into actual collision wantonly unadvisedly and maliciously with the native and on the contrary that it be no less humane than politic to leave no angry recollection of white people where the footstep of traveller however few and far between must be expect to follow yours should you route either in proceed on the expedition or return be in the direction of that part of the irwin river where for the discovery of coal the colony be indebted to yourself and brother it would be desirable that you should devote a short time to the examination of the locality where it be first find to excavation to some moderate extent in the vicinity of the vein of coal of most promise and above all to the ascertainment of the fact if coal crop out or if there be in the soil any indication of it between the place where the mine be discover by you in 1846 and the seashore in that intervene space of about thirty-eight or forty mile or to the northward of it in the direction of shark 's bay where dr von somner think the coal-seam of the irwin might again make its appearance in the event of accident occasion loss of provision and beast of burden and a necessity arise for a prompt return to the settle district you will bear in mind the cause of impediment on the march which prove so disastrous to captain gray 's party on its return from gantheaume bay the want of vigilance at night manifest in another expedition in the murder of lieutenant eyre 's european companion and the want of caution forgetfulness of the nature of barbarian and the facility for ambush afford by a wilderness of tree and jungle that have lead to injury fatal to life as in the case of mr cunningham in sir thoma mitchell 's expedition and of two of he companion at another time and in some instance as in those of captain stoke and captain gray that have lead to result all but fatal to the explorer and they expedition injury suddenly and unexpectedly inflict on individual straggle from the main body of they party or venture considerable distance in advance of it you be to bear in mind that it might be of some advantage throughout you expedition to keep a register of the depths at which water have be find by you and of those depths to same to some extent -- at least wherever appearance may lead you to expect improvement of soil a richer country or one indicate mineral production in the event of occurrence of unexpected disaster impediment and unavoidable accident arise from loss of provision or of horse or of any injury to the health or strength of the party render it utterly impracticable for the expedition to proceed as high northward as gascoyne river you discretion then supply whatever you may be unprovided for in you instruction you will explore as far as it be possible for you to do on you return the country i have the honor to be sir you obedient servant rr madden colonial secretary to ac gregory esquire perth general report of journey perth November 20 1848 sir i have the honor to transmit for the information of he excellency the governor the follow outline of the proceedings of the explore party to the northward which he excellency have be please to place under my direction i regret that we have not succeed in reach the gascoyne river which you instruction for my guidance point out as the ultimate object of the expedition but i trust that we attempt to render the expedition serviceable to the colony have not prove unsuccessful especially as the result have be the discovery of several fine portion of good grassy land near champion bay which with the more minute examination of the country in the vicinity which have be previously discover will render available a tract of pasturage sufficiently extensive to relieve the present overstocked district the estimate quantity of land suitable for depasture sheep be about 225000 acre exclusive of 100000 acre on the irwin the greater portion of which however be better suit to agricultural purpose the observation i have have the have be avoid and although there would have be many minor difficulty to encounter i feel assure that the same zeal and energy which enable my party to contend so long with the obstacle which oppose they advance to the gascoyne river would have ensure they success in a more favourable season the gentleman who form my party have my sincere thanks for they prompt and energetic co-operation on all occasion nor can i omit to mention the cheerful and trustworthy conduct of private w king of the 96th regiment for minute detail i beg to refer my journal and the plan of my route which i be plot i all salt while the man be prepare the tent etc the governor proceed to examine the vein of lead which we trace to a greater distance than on the former occasion of its discovery the water have sink two foot expose many portion of the vein which be before cover 8th December examine the lead vein trace it 320 yard in a direction north 30 degree east magnetic along the bed of the murchison river which be nearly dry clear the sand and loose stone from the surface find it to vary from eight to twenty-four inch in width the general average be twelve inch the dip to the west-north-west at a angle of about 80 degree from the horizon throughout the whole length the lead vein appear to be one solid mass of galena the northern end either terminate or alter its direction close to a vein of schistose rock which intersect the adjacent rock to the south the lode be cover by several foot of sand which prevent its be trace further as we have not time to remove it the whole of the vein which be trace be include within the bank of the river and the greater portion be cover by shallow water one specimen of galena show trace of copper the rock which prevail on each side of the vein be a hard compact gneiss abound with garnet some of which be of good color but mostly full of flaw the stratification of the gneiss be somewhat confused but it generally dip at a high angle -lrb- sometimes nearly perpendicular -rrb- to the westward the strike be north and south the facility which the position of the lode offer for mining be not very great as it occupy the lowest part of the valley and steam power would be requisite to free the mine from water and at the same time unless the small boat-harbour near the mouth of the hutt river or gantheaume bay -lrb- both within thirty mile -rrb- be find suitable for the purpose champion bay distant sixty-two mile in a direct line to the south be the nearest port where the ore could be ship in the evening the governor examine the spot where mr walcott have discover the small piece of lead ore about two and a half mile below the lode but as most of the piece have be pick up on that occasion we could only find a few fragment of it 9th December leave the encampment at 440 be and steer about south-west make we former bivouac on the hutt river about 10 pm and halted for the rest of the day 10th December start at 450 be steer 160 degree magnetic over sandy country pass a small grassy valley at 80 halt on the north branch of the bowe at 1010 on a small pool of brackish water dine and resume we route at 240 pm steer south over a grassy country till 610 when we halt for the night on a tributary stream to the bowe obtain fresh water by digging the pool be very small and brackish conflict with native governor spear 11th December leave the bivouac at 515 be steer 175 degree magnetic over a indifferent country till 640 when we cross the south branch of the bowe the country improve here we see several native who at first hide themselves but find that we see they come after we at first they do not exceed eight or ten in number but be join by several other party gradually increase till they exceed fifty when they altogether change they friendly manner and begin to bring up they spear at 615 we pass to the west of king 's table hill and as the country be cover with dense wattle thicket the native take advantage of the ground and have completely surround the party commence first to threaten to throw they spear then to throw stone and finally one man catch hold of mr bland by the arm threaten to strike he with a dowak another native throw a spear at myself though without effect but before i could fire at he the governor perceive that unless some severe example be make the whole party would be cut off fire at one of the most forward of we assailant and kill he two other shot be fire by the soldier but the thickness of the bush prevent we see with what effect a shower of spear stone kyly and dowak follow and although we move to a more open spot the native be only keep off by firing at any that expose themselves at this moment a spear strike the governor in the leg just above the knee with such force as to cause it to protrude two foot on the other side which be so far fortunate as it enable I to break off the barb and withdraw the shaft the governor notwithstanding he wound continue to direct the party and although the native make many attempt to approach close enough to reach we with they spear we be enable by keep on the most open ground and check they by a occasional shot to avoid they attack in cross the gully they follow we closely for seven mile after which they be only see occasionally follow in we track have reach the beach we be enable to travel more rapidly and although one of the pony knock up we reach champion bay at 330 pm and get the party and horse on board the champion by 50 where we be gladly welcome by lieutenant helpman about sunset the native come down to the beach conceal themselves behind the bush whilst a single unarmed native stand on the beach and call to we to come on shore no doubt in the hope of make a sudden attack on the boat should we venture to do so ac gregory assistant surveyor \*\*\* the murchison river 1857 the upper murchison river in the month of march 1857 mr surveyor ft gregory while engage on the survey of the lower part of the murchison observe that the river come down in flood though there have be no rain for several month near the coast and take advantage of such a favourable opportunity of extend the exploration of the country beyond the point at which previous explorer have be drive back for want of water and grass he proceed up the murchison accompany by he assistant mr s trigg follow the course of the river for 180 mile for the last fifty mile the condition of the vegetation show that there have be heavy rain which have cause the flood in the lower part of the river the follow be a abstract of mr gregory 's report to the surveyor-general as publish at the time in the perth gazette : -- we last week intimate that a exploratory trip have lately be make into the interior eastward of the geraldine mine we have now the pleasure and satisfaction of lay before we reader some detail of one of the most unassuming exploration yet important in its result which have ever be undertake in this colony in the latter end of march last mr assistant surveyor f gregory and mr s trigg start from the geraldine mine with two horse and sixteen pound of flour to trace the murchison to its source and return after thirteen day ' absence mr gregory have make a short report of he journey to the surveyor-general from which we have be kindly furnish with the follow extract : -- while at the geraldine mine i availed myself of the circumstance of the murchison be in flood to ascend that river and complete the sketch of the unexamined portion as also to gain any additional information that might facilitate the exploration of the country between this and the gascoyne river the fact that the native describe a considerable tract of grassy country extend northward from the head of the murchison plentifully supply with water be a additional incentive to ascertain from whence the inundation come tropical rainy season good pastoral country accompany by mr s trigg i proceed up the river about 180 mile at which point it cease to run we then ascend a hill in the vicinity of 600 or 700 foot elevation above the plain which i have since find to be beyond a doubt mount murchison of austin unfortunately i be unable to procure a copy of he map or journal and be thus prevent from lay out my route to the greatest advantage by push more to the northward and go over more new ground as it be the only information i have be able to gain beyond complete the plan of the river be that the principal fall of rain have be eastward of the 116th degree of longitude and that the tract of country between the great south bend and mount murchison which prove barely capable of support mr austin 's small party of horse in November 1854 be now yield a pasture nearly equal to the average of the champion bay district and in some part most luxuriant the grass have scarcely arrive at maturity be perfectly green this remarkable change in the character of the country be i be incline to think not entirely confine to this year in particular but that from meteorological cause this district have not unfrequently the benefit of tropical rain fall during the month of January and February although not always in sufficient quantity to cause the river to flow as low as the settle district it have already be observe by many person that during the summer month the prevailing sea breeze divide the northerly current of vapor about 100 mile inland from the west coast prevent the rain from fall throughout the same parallel of latitude as near the eastern limit of my route the murchison throw off two branch nearly equal in magnitude to the main stream i be induce to imagine that its extreme source do not lie more than sixty or seventy mile beyond that point and have it not be that i do not feel justified in abstract so large a portion of time from the regular survey of this district there be no doubt but that i could with every facility have complete the exploration of the country as far as the gascoyne in two or three week on compare the trace of the murchison which i now enclose with mr austin 's route it will be observe that there be a difference of seventeen mile in latitude and something more in longitude throughout the eastern portion a discrepancy which i be at a loss to account for as my dead-reckoning to both the outward and inward track agree well with my cross-bearing my latitudes be however take only with a pocket sextant with a treacle horizon and might therefore not be implicitly rely on i have however prefer plot my route exactly as book in the field leave the exist error to be clear up at some future period from mr trigg who arrive on Wednesday by the preston from champion bay we have gather the follow additional particulars : -- the outward route be on the south bank of the river murchison the first sixty mile be but indifferent but there be many spot of grass sufficient to maintain travel herd or flock afterwards the soil on the bank of the river improve and be continuously grassy the general width be about half a mile about latitude 26 degree 50 minute longitude 116 degree east two large branch almost if not quite equal to the main stream join the murchison from the eastward about mr austin 's mount welcome the grass be find very luxuriant -- from two to three foot high and between there and mount murchison the country be describe by mr trigg to be very beautiful and the soil superior to any he have previously see in the colony and equal to the best land in victorium mount murchison itself be a immense mass of quartz with granite round the base this differ from mr austin 's description but that gentleman do not appear to have ascend the hill from the summit three high land be observable one a isolate peak fifty mile east the other to the north and north-east apparently more distant so far as could be see the country to the east and north-east appear scrubby and indifferent the return be on the north side of the murchison and here a large extent of good grassy land be find not on the bank but a mile and a half from the river and reach four or five mile in width to the base of some hill and reach westward to the large northerly bend of the river in longitude 115 degree 30 minute about forty mile from the geraldine mine the good land in all case be very flat the soil a red loam which when dry be very open the whole country be singularly infested with white ant of which every tree living or dead appear to have its colony mr trigg regard the country around mount murchison as auriferous the striking difference there be between this account of the country on the murchison and that give by mr austin may be account for in several way : first mr austin do not appear to have cross but skirt the country intervene between mount welcome and mount murchison but he describe the land about the latter as improve and find water while it be the feed and water at mount welcome which in all probability save he party from perish the land on the north side speak of so favourably by mr trigg be not see by mr austin and also he party be so exhaust that it be out of he power to diverge from a direct line in order to examine the nature of the country on either side whereas messr gregory and trigg make such a examination whenever any favourable appearance present itself and thus determine the quantity of valuable land for a distance of six or seven mile on each side of the river and have thus be the means of confer on the colony one of the greatest benefit it have receive since the northern district be first open by mr a gregory \*\*\* gascoyne river 1858 perth to champion bay in consequence of the very satisfactory result of the exploration of the upper murchison river by messr gregory and trigg in 1857 a number of settler in the northern district subscribe horse and equipment for a explore party to examine the country still further to the east and north and with the sanction of the government the expedition be place under the command of mr ft gregory the result be the discovery of a considerable area of available country on the gascoyne and lyon river as describe in mr gregory 's journal of which the follow be a copy : -- mr f gregory 's report western australium perth July 26 1858 sir in accordance with the instruction convey in you letter of the 15th march authorise I to take command of the expedition to shark 's bay in course of organization by the northern settler i have the honor to furnish the follow report of we proceedings while in that service for the information of he excellency the governor the preliminary arrangement have be complete and the heavy portion of the store forward by sea to champion bay i leave perth on the 26th march accompany by mr jame roe as find it on my former visit the volume of water now run in the bed of the river be however at this time about the same although none of the tributary include the roderick and impey have be in flood peak be visible to-day we first observe a very beautiful convolvulus which we afterwards find to bear root like a sweet potato some of they more than a pound weight and well flavored form a very it necessary to add a few observation on subject that could not well be introduce into the body of the narrative geology of country in the first place view the geographical and geological feature in combination the tract of country contain within the 114th and 118th parallel of longitude and the 24th and 27th degree of south latitude may be consider as a inclined plane the eastern edge of which have a elevation of about 1700 foot above the level of the sea commence from the coast the first 100 mile be almost exclusively of tertiary sandstone formation which the process of denudation have in many instance convert into either stony or sandy tract rarely fertile except when subject to the influence of frequent inundation this region seldom give rise to river or watercourse the flat-topped range which be often find towards the eastern limit of this formation do not generally exceed 500 or 600 foot in altitude and be only those portion of country that have not as yet yield to the waste of time or the constant action of river which rise in the higher land more to the eastward rapidly abrade and in they onward course remove the soft and porous sandstone from they basis in the deeper valley towards the eastern edge of these sandstone thin bed of oolitic limestone contain numerous fossil shell occasionally occur also gypsum and clayey shale with other indication of the probable existence of coal in the vicinity follow the series appear a compact fine-grained amorphous sandstone have a almost flinty fracture this rock in a few mile give place to granite and gneiss frequently break up by the upheaval of whinstone and porphyritic trap hill have a elevation of from 100 to 500 foot above the plain as we proceed eastward the eruptive rock become more numerous chlorite slate vein of quartz chert and variegated jasper frequently form the summit of the most elevated hill while on the general level of the plain be occasionally find thin bed of ancient lava the river unlike most other in western australium have nearly a even fall throughout they entire length amounting on a average to six foot per mile this in a country subject to the sudden fall of almost tropical rain be what give rise to the destructive inundation already describe climate of the climate and season so little be at present know that allow all other difficulty to have be overcome it would be very hazardous to risk flock and herd beyond the head of the murchison until the country have again be visit at a different period of the year as it be probably that it have as yet only be see under the most favourable condition the fluctuation of the temperature be occasionally considerable in the middle of June it some day amount to 46 degree in six hour -- register at 7 be 36 degree and at 1 pm 82 degree ice have be see as far north as latitude 24 degree 30 minute the prevailing wind during the period of inundation appear to have be from the south-east as most of the tree blow down while the soil be in a state of saturation lay with they top to the north-west in may and June the wind range between north-east and south-east of the regularity of the return of the summer rain it be at present difficult to form a decide opinion but as far as observation would admit i be incline to think they can not be rely on with any degree of certainty to the southward of the 25th degree of latitude the period at which they fall be about January and February it be a significant fact that the grass find bury beneath the mud during these month have generally attain only to nearly half they growth area of available country with regard to the quantity and distribution of the available land it will only be necessary to observe that with the exception of 30000 or 40000 acre at the mouth of the gascoyne there be no land worth occupy for many year to come to the west of the lyon river the amount of land on this river have already be estimate at nearly 300 square mile while on the upper gascoyne and its tributary there be probably double that quantity this with the land on the murchison near mount hale would make a total of about a million of acre a very important circumstance in connection with this district be the total absence so far as we be able to observe of any of the variety of gastrolobium or euphorbium which constitute the poisonous plant so fatal to cattle and sheep in other part of the colony the means of access to the upper gascoyne and lyon be another important matter for consideration i be incline to think that this district can not be advantageously settle until the tract of country between it and the north coast have be explore and a port establish somewhere between exmouth gulf and depuch island as should the country in that direction fulfil its promise the intervene space would very quickly be fill up and the land on the gascoyne become available its distance from the north coast be about 200 mile while from port gregory or champion bay would not be less than from 340 to 360 mile -- a difference of some moment in the transport of store or produce from the lay of the country to the northward of the lyon river there do not appear to be any reason to suppose that a river of any magnitude fall into exmouth gulf as there would be hardly room for it between the source of the alma and the river flow to the north coast i can not bring my report to a conclusion without record my acknowledgment to mr jame roe for the able and effective assistance he have render I throughout the expedition the barometrical observation and management of the provision department have be especially under he charge my best thanks be also due to mr wd moore and mr c nairn who on every occasion endeavor to relieve I as much as possible from some of the many arduous duty that usually devolve on the leader of a explore party chainer fairburn and the native dugel also give general satisfaction in the performance of they respective duty i may add that to the ready cooperation and unanimity that prevail throughout the party may in no small degree be ascribe the successful issue of the undertaking i have the honor to be sir etc ft gregory assistant surveyor to the honorable the surveyor-general etc \*\*\* north-west coast 1861 origin of expedition to north-west australium the important addition to geographical discovery and the large extent of valuable pastoral country that have be find on the gascoyne river and its tributary attract the attention of a number of english capitalist interested in cotton manufacture which be then in a very depressed condition in consequence of the civil war in america it be propose to establish a new colony on the north-west coast of australium have for its special object the cultivation of cotton advantage be take of the presence of mr f gregory in london to urge on the home government and the royal geographical society the desirability of fitting out a expedition to proceed direct to the north-west coast of australium accompany by a large body of asiatic labourer and all the necessary appliance for the establishment of a colony under the advice of captain roe surveyor-general of western australium and other gentleman well acquaint with the subject the scheme be modify so as to have the country explore as a preliminary to actual settlement and for this purpose a grant of 2000 pound be obtain from the imperial government to be supplement by a equal subsidy by the colonial treasury accordingly mr gregory obtain a suitable outfit for the party in london and early in 1861 proceed to western australium to confer with the governor as to the requisite detail but owe to the delay cause by a part of the fund have to be provide by a vote of the local legislature the expedition do not finally leave fremantle until 23rd April 1861 -- nearly two month later in the season than it should have do as the rainy season in north-west australium terminate about the beginning of march the follow be a abstract of the journal and report of mr gregory to the governor of western australium : -- journal of the north-west australian explore expedition 20th April 1861 all the preliminary arrangement in perth have be complete and the store and equipment of the expedition already send on board the barque dolphin i proceed to fremantle and ship the ten horse that have it become dark pull about two mile to the south-east it gradually shoal to one foot when we ground and remain there till 11 pm when the tide be at full we pull for the ship but not see she light by 1 be on the 12th and the man be much fatigue we lay on we oar for a hour and then take a stretch for two mile to the south-south-east to get under the shelter of the south-east shore of the bay when have no anchor we lay-to till daylight by which time the boat have drift into heavy roller under the high rocky land at the south-west head of the bay the wind have rise so much that the boat be only keep afloat by keep she head to the sea as we could not observe any spot at which we could land without the risk of swamp the boat and wet we firearm we continue pull towards the ship the ebb tide enable we to reach the ship by 3 pm very thankful that we have escape what at one time appear likely to have prove a serious disaster landing effect 13th may in the morning it blow so fresh from the which be now high and dry by 8 pm the tide have rise sufficiently to admit of captain dixon 's return to the dolphin while i remain with a portion of my own party to make further examination in the 12th leave the ship with two boat and provision for the day we pull for the little cove about four mile distant bear west by north for the first three mile the sounding do not show less than three fathom with a even sandy bottom the last mile shoaling gradually to the beach the landing be easily effect as there now be but little surf the shore be find to be generally very sandy a low flat brackish water but one about eight foot deep in a hollow under a steep range of bare volcanic and granite hill not more than 200 yard from the beach be find to contain a abundant supply of good water grass be plentiful and of fine quality in the valley under the hill we principal requirement be now satisfied it only remain to bring the ship in near enough to land the horse on we return to the dolphin we find that she have be visit by two native who have paddle off on log of wood shape like canoe not hollow but very bouyant about seven foot long and one foot thick which they propel with they hand only they leg rest on a little rail make of small stick drive in on each side at first they be afraid to come on board but on friendly sign be make they ascend the ladder that have be put down for they they be both fine-looking man of about forty year of age above the middle stature one measure six foot four inch and the other five foot eight inch they hair straight and black tooth regular and general feature characteristic of the tribe on the west coast they body be rather more spare and have not on they a vestige of clothing the champion bay dialect be quite incomprehensible to they they however know the use of both biscuit and tobacco some of which be give they after remain several hour on board they take they departure for the eastern shore of the bay distant at least six mile promising by sign to repeat they visit the next day it be worthy of remark that neither of these native be circumcise or have lose the front tooth as be common on this coast further to the eastward they fearlessness and confidence in the good faith of european would lead to the impression that this be not they first acquaintance with vessel on the coast it be not far from this place that captain pp king have a visit from native similarly equip more than forty year ago while on shore to-day several new and very beautiful plant and flower be observe amongst they one in particular which without exception be the handsomest shrub i have ever see in australium in form the plant resemble a large chandelier with a series of branch spring from a center stem in set of five each on these be short erect stem a few inch apart carry five beautiful deep crimson dragon flower nearly three inch in length group like lustre produce a very gorgeous effect the leaf of the plant be elegantly form like those of the mountain ash and be of a rich green a purple flowering bean the seed of which be the size of the english horse-bean be here find in abundance and be eat by the native melon similar to those formerly see by I on the gascoyne several variety of brachychiton a small variety of the adansonium three or four different kind of convolvulus -lrb- one of which run along the accident from careless use of firearm 16th may early this morning the dolphin be move to within three mile of the cove visit yesterday and anchor in two and a half fathom at the lowest water the landing place bearing west by north by 110 be the first pair of horse be hoist out and place in the water under the counter of the cutter two other boat assist in tow we to the shore which occupy about a hour the horse on landing be scarcely able to stand from the length of time they be in the water on reach the beach a serious accident occur to mr hearson the second mate of the vessel result from the negligence of jame the farrier who notwithstanding my repeat caution to all the member of the expedition to keep snapper on the lock of the gun have omit to do so in consequence of which on its be hand out the hammer catch on the gunwale of the boat and discharge a ball through both the hip of the mate cause he to fall in the water which circumstance fortunately tend materially to stop the hemorrhage he be immediately carry to a sheltered spot and a tent pitch over he on examine the wound i find the ball have enter the right posterior pass close below the joint and take a oblique direction through the lower edge of the pelvis make its exit in front of the left thigh between the femoral artery and the principal tendon without injure either this mishap and the freshening of the breeze prevent we landing any more horse to-day the remainder of it be spend in make a camp and attend to the comfort of we wounded companion who occasion I some anxiety as the treatment must entirely devolve upon myself who possess but a very limited amount of experience in matter of this nature 17th may four more horse be safely land this morning and we be return to the vessel for another pair when a party of fourteen native make they appearance at the camp at first they come boldly up but on a gun be discharge as a signal for my recall they appear much alarmed although they would not go away we number be small i determine not to allow they to enter the camp on account of they propensity to thieve and the few that could now be spare to guard the store be insufficient to keep a constant watch on they stealthy movement i therefore try at first to make they understand that we have take possession for the present and do not want they company they be however very indignant at we endeavor to drive they away and very plainly order we off to the ship it be very evident that we forbearance be mistake for weakness and that mischief be prepare i accordingly take hold of one of the most refractory and compel he to march off at double-quick time when they all retire to some rocky hill overlook we camp from which it be necessary to dislodge they take mr brown with I we climb the first hill which make they retreat to the next rest ourselves for a few minute and take a view of the surrounding country we be just on the point of return to the camp when we observe three armed native steal down a ravine to the horse evidently with hostile intention as they ship they spear on get close enough to throw we do not however give they time to accomplish they object as we run down the hill in time to confront they on which they take to the rock see that it be now time to convince they we be not to be trifle with and to put a stop at once to what i saw would otherwise terminate in bloodshed we both take deliberate aim and fire a couple of bullet so close to the principal offender that he could hardly escape feel the effect of the fragment of lead as they split upon the rock perth 6th February 1862 appendix adopt the course which i have find most convenient on similar occasion i now proceed to offer a few remark on the general feature production and natural capability etc of the country traverse by the expedition which could not without disadvantage have be introduce into the foregoing narrative these remark have already appear at the conclusion of my report publish on the 18th November 1861 but be equally applicable to the present publication commence with its geographical and geological peculiarity that portion of the country that come under we observation consist of a succession of terrace rise inland for nearly 200 mile more or less break up by volcanic hill towards the coast the first belt average from ten to forty mile in width from the sea and be a nearly level plain slightly ascend to the southward with a elevation of from 40 to 100 foot the soil be generally either light loam or strong clay accord as it be the result of the disintegration of the granite rock that occasionally protrude above its surface or of volcanic rock of black scorium that frequently interrupt the general level hill of this nature also constitute the greater portion of the more elevated island off the coast cape lambert and the promontory that shelter the western side of nickol bay the generality of these rock do not however yield so rich a soil as might be expect from they origin this be owe to the absence of actual lava the eruptive heat have nearly be sufficient to convert the superincumbent primary and tertiary rock into a vitreous scorium have a specific gravity of 32 and be highly indestructible in its texture proceed inland for the next fifty or sixty mile be a granite country that have be originally cap with horizontal sandstone and have a elevation of about 1000 foot this range terminate to the southward in level plain of good soil the produce of the next series of more elevated country while towards the northern edge the granite and sandstone have undergo great change through the action of numerous trap dyke that have greatly disturb its surface produce metamorphic rock some resemble jasper and other highly cellular and scoriaceous in about latitude 22 degree on the meridian of nickol bay we come upon another and more elevated range trend away to the south-east have a altitude of 2500 foot above the sea this unlike the last section have a southern escarpment of 500 or 600 foot and consist of horizontal sandstone and conglomerate which have comparatively undergo little change and have a average breadth of eight or ten mile the southern flank be border by fertile valley of strong loamy clay merge gradually to the southward into stony ridge and hill some have a elevation of nearly 4000 foot the culminate point be attain at mount bruce in latitude 22 degree 30 minute from this point the country gradually fall to the ashburton the bed of which river in the same meridian as the bay be about 1600 foot above the sea and the adjoining range not above 2200 foot or about the same as the country on the gascoyne lyon and upper murchison of mineral i be unable to discover any trace except iron quartz reef occasionally traverse the country in a north-north-east and south-south-west direction or nearly the same as the mineral lode at champion bay but i could not find any instance in which this rock offer much to indicate the probable existence of gold it be far surpass in this respect by the rock on the upper murchison coal do not appear likely to be find within the limit of the country pass over unless towards the easternmost point attain by the expedition with respect to the harbor on the coast i can only speak of nickol bay and the anchorage under rosemary and the adjacent island the former i consider only second to king george 's sound as it can be enter in all weather either from the north or north-east and there be reason to believe that a safe passage exist between legendre and dolphin island lead into mermaid strait where there appear to be a excellent harbor at all season of the year the sounding towards the eastern and western shore of nickol bay take at low water show sufficient depth for vessel of considerable tonnage to lie within a cable 's length of the shore the bottom be fine sand and soft mud towards the head of the bay the water be much shallower not carry more than two fathom two mile from the shore no reef be know to exist in this bay except quite close into land in make the run survey of the western promontory i find that all to the north of sloping head be a island have a boat channel between from half a mile to a mile wide to the outer portion i therefore give the name of dolphin island the tide be tolerably regular and average sixteen foot but at the spring they rise twenty-one foot on which occasion the whole of the western promontory include the high land for several mile to the westward be entirely cut off by the sea the other opening be under enderby island -- a circumstance that greatly detract from the value of these otherwise fine harbor as it would require two mile of causeway to connect the best landing place where water be to be find with the mainland the average declination of the needle throughout this district i find to be 1 degree east the result of many amplitude and azimuth there be however in the vicinity of many of the volcanic hill great local attraction of the climate i can only say that during the five month we remain on the coast we never experience the same inconvenience from it that we frequently have do within the limit of the settle district of the colony the weather be however principally fine and the sky clear during we stay only two shower have occur -- one at the latter end of may and the other in June the meteorological register keep at nickol bay show the following result from observation take at all hour of the day and night : -- column 1 : month in which thermometer reading be record column 2 : maximum column 3 : minimum may : 80 : 65 June : 76 : 63 July : 78 : 56 August : 80 : 54 September : 83 : 65 October : 92 : 70 under the peculiar circumstance of the thermometer be place on a sandbank in the sun during the hot day in October it rise to 178 degree of fahrenheit whilst the lowest it ever fall to be up in the hill in July when it be 2 degree below freezing just before sunrise the wind continue to blow almost uninterruptedly from the east and south-east during the first four month veer to the south-south-east and south and occasionally to the north-east latterly the be observe by navigator and explorer to do about the beginning of November and continue to march amongst the natural production i would first briefly refer to the bed of the pearl oyster as they be likely to become of immediate commercial importance considerable number have be gather by the crew of the dolphin at they leisure time the aggregate value of which i be tell be between 500 and 600 pound besides pearl one of which have be value by competent person at 25 pound the limit of the bed be as yet undefined but there be good reason to believe from the position of it that with proper apparatus ship could soon be load with they sandalwood be find in small quantity very highly scented but too widely scatter to become of much importance as a article of export of indigenous fruit etc we observe the adansonium or gouty-stemmed tree of sir g gray -lrb- nearly ally to the baobab or monkey bread-fruit of southern africa -rrb- sweet and water melon similar to those formerly see by I on the lyon river but of much larger size a small gourd a wild fig well-tasted and a sweet plum very palatable be find in tolerable abundance i have already speak of the palm which grow on the bank of the fortescue they be very handsome and grow to the height of forty foot but not have bring in any specimen they have not yet be identify as to they variety tobacco do not grow so luxuriantly here as on the lyon river but the native collect it and after preparation chew it but we do not on any occasion observe they to smoke many beautiful flower be also collect which will be forward to some of the most eminent botanist to be describe and classify it now only remain for I to give a opinion on the capability of the country for colonisation it would be almost impossible to particularise the position or define the limit of country adapt for grazing purpose beyond the reference already make to they the total amount of land available for this purpose within the limit of we route i should estimate at not less than two or three million of acre and of this i may safely say 200000 be suitable for agricultural purpose the greater portion of which lie on the two flank of the hamersley range on the bank of the degrey and its tributary and on the lower sherlock of the fitness of this district for the growth of wool which on account of its be a intertropical country it be generally suppose it would be unsuitable i would remark that its elevation above the sea appear likely to obviate the objection and render it probable that sheep may not degenerate in the same way they be find to do in other tropical country at any rate flock be now be push over on to the same latitude in queensland and we do not hear of the wool-grower complain that such be the case there as to its fitness for the growth of cereal it be quite possible that wheat and barley may not come to the same degree of perfection they do in the more temperate latitudes of australium but there be no reason to doubt its capability of grow sufficient grain for the support of a numerous population what it appear more highly qualify for than anything else be the growth of cotton -- a question which at the present juncture can not be lose sight of from my personal observation of the cultivation of this plant in egypt and the attention i have recently pay to this subject while in europe i feel confident that a very considerable portion of the arable land on the degrey and sherlock be precisely the soil adapt for the production of this valuable commodity as however i purpose to make this the subject of a more lengthy paper at a future period i will not now venture to enlarge upon it as the number and disposition of the aborigine be likely to have some effect on the first settlement of a district i would give it as my opinion that these people will not prove particularly troublesome to the settler if properly and fairly treat they be not numerous and appear very willing to take employ under european and will no doubt soon be make as useful as in the other district in stature they rather exceed the usual standard some of they measure two or three inch over six foot in bring my report to a close i would wish to observe that although the result of the expedition have fall short of my sanguine hope with regard to geographical discovery and will i be afraid in some degree disappoint the anticipation of the eminent geographer who have lend they valuable aid in promote the undertaking yet i can not but hope that the large amount of additional fertile country it have bring to we knowledge will compensate in some degree for the deficiency i be however unable to refrain from again express my opinion that have not so many concurrent circumstance combine to retard the departure of the expedition until so late in the season and it have arrive on the coast at the time originally recommend by the geographical society it would in all probability have result in the full accomplishment of the object they have in view it now devolve upon I to perform the pleasing duty of record my entire satisfaction with the manner in which the whole of the member of the expedition put forward they best energy in the performance of they respective function to mr turner i be indebted for the care bestow on the management of the store department which come under he immediate charge to messr brockman and hall j mccourt and jame be due my acknowledgment for the cheerful alacrity with which they perform the duty allot to they of messr maitland brown and j harding i can not speak too highly accompany I on all the extra service upon which i be engage they have to endure privation of no ordinary description which they meet with a spirit of steady fortitude deserving of the highest praise of the valuable service render to the expedition and to science by mr p walcott i have already have occasion to refer and i sincerely hope that he talent and zeal in the pursuit of botany and natural history may meet a more substantial reward than the thanks which be justly due to he and those gentleman who have give they time and talent gratuitously in the service of they fellow-colonist to captain dixon and the officer and crew of the dolphin every praise be due for the assistance which on all occasion they promptly afford in aid the expedition and for which i gladly avail myself of the present opportunity to return they my best thanks in conclusion permit I to tender you excellency my acknowledgment for the readiness with which you have accede to my various for explore northern australium and the special object of the imperial government in undertake it be best detail in the follow despatch from he grace the duke of newcastle secretary of state for the colony to captain fitzgerald governor of western australium : -- the honorable the secretary of state for the colony to the governor of western australium down street 31st August 1854 sir you will probably have be render aware by the report of the parliamentary debate of last session and from other source that she majesty 's government have be long consider the project of despatch a explore expedition to lay open if favor with success more of the interior of the great australian continent than the many energetic but partial attempt hitherto make have succeed in develop this scheme originate with the council of the royal geographical society who correspond with the colonial department on the subject of it during last winter but it be ultimately consider by she majesty 's government that the importance of the subject render it more advisable that the expedition should be undertake under they own superintendence and as a matter of public concern and parliament have now place at they disposal a sum of 5000 pound for the purpose and will undoubtedly give further assistance should it be requisite great difficulty have however present themselves as to the necessary arrangement the hostility in which the country be involve have necessarily direct the time and thought not of she majesty 's government only but also of many of those whose professional knowledge and experience might have be of the greatest assistance in another direction of the distinguished australian explorer now in this country some be incapacitate by reason of health and other by the circumstance of they service be require in other direction from take the command it would however be a matter of regret if now that the money have be vote and the preparation partially make the expedition be not able to start at the best period for commence operation next year which on the northern coast of australium seem generally think to be from February to April i enclose copy of certain portion of the correspondence which take place early in the present year between the colonial department and captain stoke and mr sturt who be consult in order to obtain the benefit of they advice and the former of whom i have at one time the hope to secure for the command of the expedition you will collect from these document that the general view of those who have consider the subject appear to be that moreton bay would be a convenient rendezvous for the land portion of the expedition that they might be convey by sea to the mouth of the victorium river on the north-west coast that it would be advantageous if possible that they should act in concert with a government vessel which might be employ in survey operation in the gulf of carpentarium and neighborhood while the land explorer be engage in the interior selection of commander she majesty 's government be however fully aware that such project especially where they involve so much combination can only be submit generally to the leader of such a expedition to whom great latitude must be leave as to the mode of carry he instruction into execution they have now come to the determination of offer the command of the land expedition to mr ac gregory assistant surveyor in western australium they have be induce to take this course both by the very high testimonial which have be give to the ability and fitness of this gentleman for the purpose by such authority as they have be able to consult in england and also by you own report concern he particularly that contain in you despatch of the 6th January 1852 should mr gregory accept the charge which i trust notwithstanding its arduous and responsible nature you will find he ready to do it be the wish of she majesty 's government that without wait for further instruction he should proceed immediately to sydney where he will find such instruction await he and where he party will be organise you be authorise to supply mr gregory with the necessary fund for this purpose which will be repay to the local government from the commissariat chest if you be aware of any person in you government well qualify and willing to serve under mr gregory in subordinate capacity or if he have himself any assistant whom he would be anxious to engage you be at liberty to place they at he disposal but it must be understand that this permission do not apply to person who be to take charge of scientific department of the expedition as there be already gentleman of this class with whom she majesty 's government have be in correspondence any such person who may wish to join the expedition can do so only as a volunteer copy of this despatch have be transmit by the same mail to sir charle fitzroy and likewise to the other australian governor sir charle fitzroy will therefore be fully prepare to receive mr gregory and to render he all assistance in he power and i have every reason to hope for the zealous co-operation of the several local legislature and government in a scheme intend for the development of the vast and unknown resource of they common continent you will on receive this despatch immediately communicate with mr gregory and if he should accept the command of the expedition inform both the secretary of state for the colony and sir charle fitzroy and the other australian government immediately of he have do so and of he intended movement i have etc -lrb- sign -rrb- newcastle journal of the north australian explore expedition by ac gregory the preliminary arrangement for the north australian explore expedition be complete the store equipment and a portion of the party be embark at sydney in the barque monarch and schooner tom tough and sail for moreton bay on the 18th July 1855 and on the 22nd anchor at the bar of the brisbane river the next day the monarch attempt to enter the river but be take by the government pilot half a mile to the east of the channel over the bar ground and be not get off till the 26th when she enter the river the steamer ballarat be engage to tow the monarch up to the town of brisbane but have strike on a rock near ipswich sink and the steamer hawk be engage to tow up the river the hawk however prove to be of insufficient power and it be then decide to embark the horse and sheep which have be collect by mr hc gregory at eagle farm horse embark at moreton bay the horse have be get on board the monarch on the 31st July and the sheep the next day the steamer bremer be employ to tow she over the bar it be evident however that the bremer do not intend to do this for she slack the tow-line and then steam ahead full speed and snap the hawser and go off without any explanation have remove a quantity of store from the monarch to the tom tough so as to reduce the draft of the former on the 8th August warped over the bar and go over to moreton island where about three ton of water be take in from the fresh-water creek near the pilot station on the 12 August weigh and leave moreton bay and this be the last point of communication with the civilised world the expedition might be consider to commence on this date the party consist of eighteen person as follow : commander ac gregory assistant commander hc gregory geologist j wilson artist and storekeeper j baine surgeon and naturalist jr elsey botanist f mueller collector and preserver j flood overseer g phibb stockmen etc c humphry r bowman c dean j melville w dawson w shewell w selby s macdonald h richard j fahey the livestock comprise fifty horse and 200 sheep the provision consist of flour salt pork preserved beef rice pea preserve potato sago sugar tea coffee vinegar limejuice etc calculate to supply the party on full ration for eighteen month on 13th August pass breaksea spit and port curti next morning the weather be fine with south-east wind reach port albany on 26th land on albany island which be principally of sandstone formation rise into hill of moderate elevation the soil generally poor and sandy cover with bush and small tree with a few open grassy patch fresh water be find in a small cove 100 yard north from the landing-place on the sandy beach the supply be so small as to be of little use and the position inconvenient of access the mainland appear to be cover with much dense bush and the rocky sandstone hill do not indicate that the country be of any great value either for agricultural or pastoral purpose port albany be a narrow but deep channel between albany island and the mainland of cape york it be easy of ingress and egress but be neither safe or convenient owe to the great rapidity of the current which set through with the tide some canoe with native come to the vessel they evidently have frequent communication with vessel pass through the strait and be well acquaint with the use and name of tobacco which they smoke in large bamboo pipe they arm consist of spear bow and arrow the canoe form of a single tree rudely hollow out and fit with outrigger 27th August leave port albany and pass through endeavor strait be favor with a light easterly wind as far as port essington which be sight on September 1st and after pass through dunda strait anchor for the night the follow morning pass vernon island with a light breeze at 950 pm the monarch ground on a rocky reef off the entrance of port patterson the master of the vessel not have make due allowance for the indraught of the tide unfortunately this occur at the top of the spring tide and the result be that though every exertion be make to warp the vessel off the tide do not rise sufficiently to float she until the 10th September when by cut off the false keel and level the surface of the rock we succeed in haul she off with comparatively little damage as the weather continue calm during the whole of this anxious period as the vessel lay on she side at low tide the position of the horse be extremely inconvenient and they suffer a greater amount of injury during these eight day than on the whole of the precede voyage and it be to this that the subsequent loss of so large a number of the horse be to be attribute for though only two die on board the vessel the other become so excessively weak that some have not the strength to go through the fatigue of landing and the journey from point pearce to the victorium river and at the same time the supply of forage be so reduce that it become necessary to land the horse immediately on reach point pearce and before the place could be examine for the best landing land at the entrance of victorium river after get off the reef light wind and calm delay the voyage to the victorium river but as the tom tough work along the coast better than the monarch i go on with the schooner to examine the entrance of the river ascend the victorium to blunder bay find that the locality be not suit for landing horse and therefore return to treachery bay near which mr hc gregory have discover abundance of grass and water under providence hill of captain stoke commence land the horse on the 18th but in consequence of the strong tide and extensive mangrove flat great difficulty be encounter the horse have to swim more than two mile from the vessel to the shore and be so exhaust that three be drown one lose in the mud and mangrove and one go mad and rush into the bush and be lose have transfer the store to the tom tough on the 24th the monarch sail for singapore mr wilson be instruct to proceed in the schooner up the victorium river and to establish a camp at the highest convenient position on the bank of the river while i proceed overland with mr h gregory dr mueller and seven of the man hope by easy journey of eight to ten mile per day to give the horse time to partially recover the effect of the voyage macadam range run stream of fresh water 1st October 1855 accompany by mr h gregory i leave the camp to search for a practicable route by which we could cross the macadam range but after proceed about a mile shoot a emu with which we return to camp and again start at 710 be pursue a south-east course cross a stony ridge and at 80 be come on a creek about twenty yard wide with good pool of water and a grassy margin but the country generally barren and stony after several ineffectual attempt we ascend the hill to the south-east of the creek and traverse a very broken country of sandstone formation till 110 be when we reach the head of a creek trend to the southward this be follow down till 10 pm when we halt a hour and again proceed till 430 pm the country be very poor and rise into rocky hill on both bank of the creek we then enter a wide grassy flat destitute of tree extend six mile north to south and fifteen mile east to west on the south side there appear to be a creek or river which we suppose to be the fitzmaurice river this plain be bound on all side by steep rocky hill of sandstone of barren aspect return up the creek till 60 pm and halted for the night the day be hot and sultry though a heavy thundershower somewhat cool the air the macadam range be of sandstone the stratum of which dip about 30 degree to the south in which direction as we advance the rock be more slaty and break into rhomboidal fragment water be abundant in the creek but the grass be scanty and the rough surface of the sandstone and rocky ravine render the country difficult to traverse timber be scarce chiefly small-sized eucalyptus the cotton-tree be observe in a few of the valley 2nd October return to the camp we attempt to follow one of the creek down to the plain on the north-west side of the range but find the ravine too steep and rocky for the horse to pass and be compel to retrace we step and cross several steep and rocky hill reach the camp at 20 pm at which time the thermometer stand at 94 degree in the shade and 114 degree in the sun 3rd October three of the horse have stray and this detain we till 110 be when i start with the party leave mr h gregory and bowman to look for the missing animal proceed in a south-east direction to the cross of the first creek ascend the macadam range and steer east-south-east to the second creek the course be then north-east and east to the head of the creek tributary to the fitzmaurice river and then encamp at 345 pm at the highest point on this day 's route the aneroid stand at 2940 and at the camp 2955 thermometer 88 degree the higher point of the range do not exceed 100 before the highest ridge cross by a meridian altitude of a cygnus the latitude 14 degree 33 minute 26 seconds 4th October at 100 be messr h gregory and bowen reach the camp with one of the miss horse and have obtain some provision return to search for the other two horse at noon start with the party and follow down the creek in a south-south-east direction till 4 pm and encamp at the termination of the hilly country one of the horse madman show symptom of illness a short time before we start and in cross the creek half a mile above where we encamp he fall down and in less than three minute die this be a serious loss as this animal be one of the most serviceable of we horse have stand the voyage without lose he condition the cause of death we be unable to ascertain but the probability be that some poisonous plant exist at the place where we encamp last night by a meridian altitude of a cygnus the latitude of the camp be 14 degree 39 minute 26 seconds thinly timbered with white-gum eucalyptus of small size and nearly destitute of leaf and though the whole country be grassy it be so much parch by the intense heat that it present a very sterile October resume we journey down the creek at 70 be the general course south-south-west the country become so steep and rocky that at 80 we leave the valley and steer south cross several stony hill with rocky ravine which be so rugged that they be scarcely passable at 110 sight the victorium river about six mile below kangaroo point but on attempt to descend the range be intercept by a deep valley bound by sandstone cliff 50 to 100 foot high follow the valley to the east and north-east in search of a break by which we could descend but without success at 30 pm one of the horse be so completely exhaust that he could proceed no farther i therefore halt the party and be examine the cliff to ascertain the best place for lower one of the party by a rope into the valley for the purpose of procure water from the pool which be visible 300 foot below we when i find a small spring on the top of the cliff at which we encamp as soon as the horse be unsaddled mr h gregory and myself proceed to examine the valley to the east but have not go more than a mile when we observe a column of smoke rise from the camp follow by a sheet of flame which extend in a few seconds to the side of the adjacent hill we therefore return to the camp to subdue the fire and if possible save some of the grass for the horse which with great difficulty we succeed in do but though check the fire have extend many mile over the country and keep we busy all night this fire originate for want of due precaution in clear the grass around the fire at the camp though the cook have be caution on the subject 17th October at 50 be leave the camp with mr h gregory and recommence the search for a practicable descent into the valley and about two mile from the camp find a break in the cliff the hill be however so steep and rocky that it be necessary to form a path for the horse and while mr h gregory return and be bring up the party from the camp i employ myself in fill up chasm with stone and remove rock from the path the steepness of the declivity greatly facilitate they removal as it require but little force to hurl rock of several ton weight into the valley below fortunately we accomplish the descent without any accident and reach the base of the hill at 1130 be descend the creek which occupy the lower part of the valley for about two mile encamp at a small pool of water i then ride down the bank of the victorium river and ascertain that we be about six mile below kangaroo point return to the camp procure fresh horse and accompany by mr h gregory proceed to kangaroo point reach the spot be doubtful whether the vessel have proceed up the river i decide on continue we route to some convenient spot for a camp near steep head and accordingly return to the party the southern face of sea range be very abrupt and surmount by a cliff of red sandstone 50 to 100 foot high the whole height of the hill about 500 foot the range be the edge of a elevated tableland the upper stratum be hard sufficient to enable it to form a channel to the north-west coast be show by the barometric measurement : the divide ridge between the head of the victorium and hooker 's creek be about 1200 foot at -lrb- which appear the most probable outlet -rrb- be 370 mile and allow a increase of 500 for deviation there would be more than two foot descent per mile which would be sufficient for the maintenance which have be lay on the shingle bank near the dome to complete repair i be glad to learn that all the man belong to the expedition be in good health except richard whose hand be still in a very be leave at the camp to be under the immediate care of the medical officer this great amount of sickness be owe to the combined effect of previous disease and the inferior quality of the provision with which the vessel be supply it appear that through damage by salt water and want of good management the provision which should have be sufficient for two year be now reduce to salt beef of inferior quality and tea the expedition have have to furnish flour rice sugar pea and pork as also medical store for the sick man in consequence of the reduce number of the crew of the tom tough mr wilson have find it necessary to furnish man to assist in work the schooner as well as to effect repair 10th may much of the grass near the camp have be burnt i send the horse to the creek three mile above the camp party employ in general duty of the camp twenty-nine sheep remain they be now in fair condition the average weight forty to forty-five pound they would probably have be much fatter have they be judiciously shepherd but they have be keep close to the camp where the feed have be eat off closely the native have be frequently at the camp in small party and on these occasion be very quiet in they demeanor but have make hostile demonstration when meet by small detach party of the expedition and on one occasion mr wilson have deem it necessary to fire at they but only one of the black should proceed to the gulf of carpentarium via coupang in the island of timor where a supply of rice and sugar can be procure for the expedition and the vessel will be enable to complete she store it appear desirable that the land party should refit with all possible despatch for the journey to the gulf of carpentarium in order to take advantage of the cool season and there be reason to expect that the horse will be sufficiently recruit in strength towards the end of June i be therefore in hope that the party will be able to leave the victorium before the expiration of the ensue month a
