assembly dr leichhardt propose expedition in search of order by the legislative assembly to be print 28th October 1857 proceedings of the executive council on the 14th September 1857 with respect to a expedition in search of dr leichhardt minute number 57-44 he excellency the governor-general at the instance of the honorable the colonial secretary bring under the consideration of the council a proposal which have be make to organise another expedition to ascertain if possible beyond doubt the fate of dr leichhardt who leave sydney some nine year ago with the intention of explore the north-western interior of australium this proposal have its origin in a public meeting hold in sydney on the 11th instant at which resolution be pass invoke the assistance of the government and it be recommend to favourable consideration at the present moment by the circumstance that mr gregory who recently return from a successful exploration in the same direction have intimate he willingness to undertake the conduct of the propose expedition 2 the council express themselves desirous of seize so favourable a opportunity of pursue this inquiry and they therefore advise that mr gregory should be at once invite to submit for approval a definite proposal have for its object : 1st to ascertain the fate of the late dr leichhardt and 2nd to connect the explore survey of mitchell and kennedy with he own such proposal to be accompany by a estimate of the probable expense which it will be necessary to incur edward c merewether clerk of the council executive council office sydney 22 September 1857 ac gregory esquire to the colonial secretary sydney 15 September 1857 sir adverting to you verbal communication of yesterday with reference to the propose expedition in search of trace of dr leichhardt i have the honor to furnish a memorandum of the arrangement i would suggest for the organization and conduct of a party calculate to effect the object in view together with a estimate of the probable cost these document i have submit to such of the gentleman compose the committee of the leichhardt association as i have have the opportunity of consulting and i have avail myself of they experience of the district in which the expedition would be organise although i have allow extreme rate for many of the item of expenditure yet as in all undertaking of this description unavoidable and unforeseen contingency be certain to arise i should scarcely feel justified in name the gross amount which should be available though not necessarily expend at a less sum than 4500 pound i have etc ac gregory the honorable the colonial secretary memorandum for the organization of a explore expedition for the purpose of search for trace of dr leichhardt 's party the object of the propose expedition would be primarily to search for trace of dr leichhardt and he party who start from the settle district of new south wale in April 1848 with the intention of proceed to western australium and if possible to ascertain the fate of that unfortunate explorer secondly the examination of the country both in the intervene space between the track of previous explorer and also beyond the limit of that hitherto explore with a view of develop its resource especially with reference to its capability for settlement the party despatch by the colonial government under mr hely in 1851-2 trace dr leichhardt to a spot near the head of the warrego river beyond this spot dr leichhardt have express he intention of proceed down the victorium river to its northern bend and then shape he course along the interior slope of the range which he suppose exist at the source of the stream flow to the northern coast the propose route of the search expedition would therefore be to reach leichhardt 's last known camp and then to examine the bank of the victorium river to the junction of the alice river at the northern bend where especial search would be make as dr leichhardt intend to leave letter there and would probably encamp for several day to recruit before finally enter the unknown country and the non-existence of mark at this point would be almost conclusive evidence that the party have perish nearer to the settlement in the search for trace of the miss party beyond this point -lrb- as it could only be at the camping place that any trace would remain after so long a interval -rrb- it would be necessary to follow such natural feature as would probably have influence the party in the selection of its route assume that the general course would be north-west the junction of the alice with the victorium river 370 mile not allow for deviation the party to consist of two section which may be term the explore and the auxiliary party the first would comprise eight person equip and provision for 5 month and for the conveyance of which 32 horse would be require as follow : commander assistant overseer etc 4 stockman 1 aboriginal stockman the second section would be compose of six person provision etc for 2 month and for the conveyance of which 13 horse would be require as follow : 1 leader 4 stockman 1 aboriginal black these two section would proceed together to the junction of the alice and victorium river and would be sufficiently strong to detach party to examine point out of the more direct line of route which the main body would follow on reach the spot above refer to the explore party would be fit out in the most efficient manner for continue its operation by select the strongest and most serviceable portion of the horse equipment etc while the auxiliary party would return with the remainder to the settlement thus afford nearly all the advantage of a depot without incur the greater expense or inconvenience attend the otherwise necessary return of the explore party by the same route it be scarcely necessary to advert to the many advantage which would be derive from this arrangement for enable the explore party to reach the extreme known point of country with its strength impair in the least possible degree while it would afford a opportunity of test the capability of the party to be finally select estimate of the cost -lrb- in wale expedition in search of dr leichhardt report of proceedings order by the legislative assembly to be print 1 September 1858 report of the proceedings of the expedition in search of dr leichhardt and party 8th December 1857 to 11th January 1858 have receive instruction from the honorable the secretary for land and public work to organise a expedition for the purpose of search for trace of dr leichhardt and party who leave new south wale in 1848 with the intention of proceed overland to western australium i proceed to moreton bay with such portion of the equipment as have be prepare in sydney on reach ipswich forty horse be purchase and have despatch the store to mr royd 's station on the dawson river by dray the party be collect at that place but owe to unforeseen delay in the transport of the store the equipment and organization of the expedition be not complete till the latter part of march the follow list of the party horse store etc will show the principal arrangement the party consist of nine person namely : commander ac gregory assistant commander cf gregory assistant s burgoyne overseer g phibb stockmen etc r bowman w selby t dunn w von wedel and d worrell the stock consist of horse alone comprise thirty-one pack and nine saddle horse completely equipped provision comprise the dry meat of two bullock and four sheep weigh as butcher 's meat 16 hundredweight but when dry and the bone remove reduce to 300 pound in addition to this 500 pound bacon 1600 pound flour 100 pound rice 350 pound sugar 60 pound tea 40 pound tobacco and some minor article the arm and ammunition be : one minie rifle eight double-barrel gun nine revolver pistol 25 pound gunpowder 150 pound shoot and ball percussion cap etc for the conveyance of water two leather water-bag be provide each hold five gallon besides which each of the party be furnish with a water-bag of india-rubber hold three pint the tent be make of calico each suit for the accommodation of two person and the several article of camp equipage be of the lightest construction consistent with the service require the instrument employ be a eight-inch sextant box-sextant prismatic compass pocket compass double axis compass aneroid barometer thermometer and artificial horizon etc include forty set of horse-shoe farrier 's and carpenter 's tool together with sundry material for repair etc the total weight of the equipment be about 4600 pound exclusive of the saddle and harness which give a average load of 150 pound as the net load carry by each pack-horse the party start from juanda station 24th march to 27th march these arrangement be complete the expedition leave juanda and proceed by the road to mr cardew 's station at euroomba from which under the guidance of mr bolton -- whose local knowledge be of material service -- we make we way through the dense scrub and broken country to the west for about thirty mile to the head of scott 's creek a small tributary of the dawson river 29th march the general course be now west-north-west through a country with rich grassy valley and dense scrub of brigalow acacia on the higher ground green grass be abundant at this time but i fear that in season of drought few of the waterhole be permanent the timber consist of ironbark box and a few other species of eucalyptus -- the brigalow acacia attain the height of thirty foot soft brown sandstone of the coal measure be the prevail rock form hill with table summit 2nd April with some difficulty owe to the dense scrub we cross the basaltic ridge which divide the eastern water flow to the dawson river from those trend to the west into the basin of the maranoa river a tributary of which -- probably the merivale river -- be follow westward the country become more sandy timbered with ironbark cypress etc the whole be however well grassed and suit for grazing if not too heavily stock 5th April reach the maranoa river in about latitude 25 degree 45 minute water be scarcely procurable in the sandy bed and we have to dig well to obtain a supply 7th April to 12th April warn by the fact that messr h gregory and haly have be unable to penetrate the country to the west from scarcity of water even three month earlier in the season we follow up the maranoa to mount owen and have find a sufficient supply of water and grass for a few day ' halt i proceed to reconnoitre the country to the west and at length find a practicable route to the tributary of the warrego river to which the party be advance a heavy shower of rain have fill the gully in this locality and green grass clothe the country form a striking contrast to the dry and waterless valley of the maranoa 15th to 16th April fine openly timbered valley well suit for pasture alternate with ridge of scrub of brigalow acacia till we reach mount playfair a basaltic hill on the sandstone ridge which separate the warrego valley from that of the nive a small branch of which be follow down to its junction with the main channel in latitude 25 degree 6 minute the soil in the valley of the nive be sandy thinly grass and openly timbered with ironbark spot gum etc the back country rise into low sandstone ridge cover with dense scrub of brigalow acacia some pool of permanent water contain small fish be pass on the bank of which the remains of numerous native camp be see 17th April from the nive river a north-north-west course be pursue through a nearly level sandy country cover with a scrub of acacia eucalyptus bottle-tree etc which offer great impediment to we progress till within six mile of the victorium river when we suddenly emerge from the scrub on to open downs of rich clay soil but the drought have be of such a long continuance that the whole of the vegetation have be destroy and sweep away by the wind leave the country to all appearance a absolute desert the bed of the victorium be scarcely ten yard wide and perfectly dry so that it be only after a prolonged search along its course that a small puddle of water be find in a hollow of the clay flat and near it fortunately for we horse a little grass grow in widely scatter tuft the barcoo river 19th April be now on the line of route which dr leichhardt have state he intention of follow the party be divide so that both side of the river be examine in all probable position in which he camp might have be situate but as the high flood appear to have inundate the country for nearly a mile on each bank last year all track of previous explorer be necessarily obliterate and it be only by marked tree or the bone of cattle that we could hope to discover any trace during the first two day ' journey down the river only a few small pool of water be see and these not of a permanent character while the rich vegetation on the open downs which have excite the admiration of sir t mitchell on he discovery of the country in a favourable season have wholly pass away leave little but a bare surface of clay the deep fissure in its surface give evidence of long-continued drought 20th April in latitude 24 degree 37 minute longitude 146 degree 13 minute a small sandy creek of equal size with the victorium join from the east and just below the first permanent pool of water be find there be a slight improvement in the grass but dense scrub prevail in the back country and even approach the river at interval leichhardt 's marked tree 21st April while collect the horse near this pool of water i detect a party of armed native watch one of the stockman evidently from they position in the scrub and general movement incline to hostility and i imagine that it be a knowledge that we be aware of they intention which prevent my be able to establish any communication with they i may here remark that this party which number about eight be the first native see during the journey continue we route along the river -lrb- latitude 24 degree 35 minute longitude 36 degree 6 minute -rrb- we discover a moreton-bay ash -lrb- eucalyptus sp -rrb- about two foot in diameter mark with the letter l on the east side cut through the bark about four foot from the ground and near it the stump of some small tree which have be cut with a sharp axe also a deep notch cut in the side of a sloping tree apparently to support the ridge pole of a tent or some similar purpose all indicate that a camp have be establish here by leichhardt 's party the tree be near the bank of a small reach of water which be note on sir t mitchell 's map this together with its actual and relative position as regard other feature of the country prove it not to have be either one of sir t mitchell 's or mr kennedy 's camp as neither encamp within several mile of the spot besides which the letter could not have be mark by either of they to designate the number of the camp as the former have long pass he fiftieth camp and the latter have not reach that number on the outward route and number he camp from the farthest point attain on he return journey notwithstanding a careful search no trace of stock could be find this be however easily account for as the country have be inundate last season though the current have not be sufficiently strong to remove some emu bone and mussel shell which lay round a native camping place within a few yard of the spot no other indication have be find we continue the search down the river examine every likely spot for marked tree but without success the general aspect of the country be extremely level and even the few distant ridge which be visible have but small elevation above the plain the highest apparently not exceed 200 or 300 foot timber be wholly confine to the bank of the river and though open plain exist acacia scrub be the principal feature water become very scarce in the channel of the river and we be principally dependent on small puddle of rainwater from a recent thunder-shower but as we approach the northern bend some fine reach of water be pass the alice river 6th April to 28th April in latitude 26 degree 2 minute we observe a small dry creek join from the north-east this i trace upward for a few mile but as its relative position with regard to the adjacent country as well as the latitude do not correspond with that of the alice river on the chart we continue we route find however that the general course of the river change to south-west i leave the party at a small lagoon and ride up the river again make a second search more especially at the junction of the small dry creek which prove to be identical with the alice river though more than five mile to the south as the victorium river never reach the parallel of 24 degree we position be now become very critical as a long continuance of drought have not only dry up all the water except in the deepest hollow in the channel of the main river but the smaller vegetation and even the tree on the back country be annihilate render the country almost impracticable from the quantity of fall dead branch and even in the bed of the river where the inundation derive from heavy rain near the source of the river last year have somewhat refresh the grass it be scarcely possible to find subsistence for the horse under exist circumstance it would have be certain destruction to attempt a north-west route from this point and the only course that appear open to we be to follow down the main river to the junction of the thompson river and ascend that watercourse so as to intersect leichhardt 's probable line of route have he penetrate in that direction favor by a better season at the same time it be probable that like ourselves he have be repulse and would then follow down the river and search for a more favourable point from which to commence he north-west course in order to round the desert interior on its northern side and we therefore continue we search down towards the thompson river 29th April to 2nd may the country be perfectly flat on both side of the river and show trace of tremendous flood the soil near the river be often deeply-cracked mud water very scarce and grass seldom see the back country be cover with scrub of dead acacia the soil a red sand or gravel and such be the unpromising appearance that i begin to fear that we horse would soon fail for want of food and water but have camp at a waterhole during Sunday to rest the party heavy rain commence and though the greater portion of the water be absorb by the dry soil some of the channel of the river fill and commence to flow this relieved we from much difficulty as regard the want of water and enable we to seek for grass in position which be otherwise inaccessible 3rd may just as we be leave we camp a party of seven native make they appearance but though they come up to we and talk much i could get no useful information from they as the party move on they follow we and think they be not observe make a attempt to throw a spear at one of the man but mr c gregory wheeling he horse quickly and present a revolver at the intend aggressor they run away and leave we to pursue we journey in peace the thompson river 4th may to 6th may the abundance of water be not without its inconvenience and have the rain continue the party would have be annihilate as we camp be between the deep channel which intersect the plain and in attempt to extricate ourselves from the plain subject to inundation find ourselves so completely entangled among the numerous deep channel and boggy gully in some of which the horse narrowly escape suffocation in the soft mud that after have ford one branch of the river carry the whole equipment across on we own back construct a bridge over a second for the transport of the store and drag the horse through as we best could with rope after three day of severe toil we have scarcely accomplish a direct distance of five mile the dry weather which follow rapidly harden the surface of the clay plain and i attempt to steer due west to the thompson but find the country so destitute of feed and cover with dense acacia scrub that we be compel to return to the plain on the bank of the river 8th may the valley of the river trend west be somewhat contract and do not exceed five or six mile in breadth the plain be firmer salt-bush and grass more abundant and the horse recover slightly from the effect of the barren country keep back from the right bank of the main channel we pass some ridge of drift sand and come on a fine lagoon nearly a mile in length here we surprise a party of native who decamp on we approach leave a net fish etc which we of course leave untouched and camp at a spot lower down the lagoon 9th may the next day be Sunday we remain at we camp and the party of native consist of seven or eight man three or four woman and some child approach we and remain the greater part of the day near the tent they be very anxious to enter the camp but this be not permit by sign they express that they have observe we have not take away any of they property the evening before when they run away and leave they net and be therefore satisfied we intention be friendly but we could not procure any information relative to the object of we journey or the character of the country before we at 4 pm they inform we they be go to sleep at the most distant part of the lagoon and would return next morning at sunrise and then depart after dark however the native be detect attempt to crawl into the camp through the bush and though we call to they in a unmistakable tone to retire they would not withdraw as the position they have take up be such as to command we camp and render it unsafe in the event of a attack it be necessary to dislodge they i therefore fire a pistol over they but be answer by a shout of derision which no doubt would have be soon follow by a shower of spear have we not compel they to retreat by a discharge of small shot direct into the scrub after which we be not further molest 10th may we be now approach the junction of the thompson river but the country become worse as we advance and the last five mile of the plain be absolutely devoid of vegetation we hope be however raise on finding that the late rain have cause the thompson to flow though the current be not strong we have however to travel upward of twelve mile up its course before any grass could be find for the horse 11th may continue we route up the thompson nothing could be more desolate than the aspect of the country except the few tree which grow on the immediate bank of the river there be scarcely a tree leave alive while the plain be quite bare of vegetation except a few salsolaceous bush at the distance of five mile low ridge of red drift sand show the desert character of all around even the lower surface of the cloud assume a lurid tinge from the reflection of the bare surface of red sand 12th to 15th may in latitude 24 degree 40 minute low sandstone hill or rather tableland approach both bank of the river and the gully which intersect they have supply the water lower down as the channel be dry above we however succeed in reach latitude 23 degree 47 minute when the absence of water and grass -- the rain not have extend so far north and the channel of the river separate into small gully and spread on the wide plain -- preclude we progress further to the north or west and the only prospect of save we horse be to return south as quickly as possible this be a most severe disappointment as we have just reach the part of the country through which leichhardt most probably travel if the season be sufficiently wet to render it practicable thus compel to abandon the principal object of the expedition only two course remain open -- either to return to the head of the victorium river and attempt a northern course by the valley of the belyando or to follow down the river and ascertain whether it flow into cooper 's creek or the darling the latter course appear most desirable as it be just possible that leichhardt under similar circumstance have be drive to the south-west in order to ascertain whether any large watercourse come from the west the return route be along the right bank of the thompson but only one small creek and some inconsiderable gully join on that side nor be the country of a better character than on the left bank -- consist of barren plain subject to inundation low rocky ridge cover with dense scrub and sandy ridge produce triodium 22nd to 23rd may we have nearly reach the victorium river when in cross a gully worrell 's horse fall and hurt he so severely that we have to halt for some time before he could be place on he horse again and it be therefore fortunate that a small patch of dry grass be find on the bank of the river which enable we to halt the next day which be Sunday travel down the right bank of the river the principal channel be full of water but the clay plain between be quite dry the rain which have cause the river to flow not have extend so far south nothing could well be more desolate than the unbounded level of these vast plain which destitute of vegetation extend to the horizon we horse be reduce to feed on the decayed weed and even these be so scarce that they eagerly devour the thatch of some old native hut 27th may we have nearly reach the furthest point attain by mr kennedy when the horse show sign of fail strength and the channel on the east side of the plain be dry i conceive it prudent to cross to the western side again the dry mud be so deeply crack that the horse be continually fall and one horse be so completely exhaust that we have to abandon he kennedy 's marked tree 28th may steer a westerly and then a north course we reach the small waterhole at mr kennedy 's second camp on the return route there be just sufficient water to supply the party for one night and a few scattered tuft of grass near it but quite insufficient for the supply of so large a number of horse close to the waterhole we find mr kennedy 's marked tree it be a large box-tree mark on the north side thus : k ii the cut of the axe and chisel be still quite clear though twelve year have elapse but the slow growth and decay of tree in the interior may be attribute to the dryness of the climate 29th may steer north-west after toiling nearly thirty mile across this fearful waste of dry mud we at length reach a small patch of grass on a sandy hummock but only just in time to save the horse as many could scarcely keep on they leg and we have to remove they load to those which be less exhaust 30th may long before the next morning we hungry animal have consume every blade of grass and the small patch round the camp be reduce to the same barren appearance as the surround plain we therefore start in search of food for they and be fortunate in find a second patch of grass about three mile to the south and halted for the remainder of the day which be Sunday thankful that providence have enable we to make it a day of rest plain of dry mud 31st may the run channel of the river be still to the west of we position we steer south-west over barren clay plain to some low ridge of drift sand beyond which we find the channel full of water with a slight current but it terminate in a large reach of water which have not yet fill and the channel lower down be dry low ridge of red drift sand be now frequent on the plain and appear to be the higher point of the former sandy desert the clay plain result from the deposition of mud in the hollow between which have in course of time fill it to one uniform level latitude 26 degree 2 minute 1st June the channel on the western side of the plain be very irregular sometimes completely lose on the level surface and again collect into large hollow with box-tree on the bank in which fine sheet of water still remain some 100 yard wide and more than a mile in length we therefore do not experience so much inconvenience with regard to the supply of this necessary element as from the absence of sufficient grass and the all but impracticable nature of the mud plain 4th June in latitude 27 degree low sandstone tableland approach the west side of the river and we attempt to travel along the slope between it and the mud plain but find it so stony that the horse ' hoof be soon worn to the quick as we have be compel to remove they shoe to enable they to traverse the mud plain have it not be for green bush of salsola and some similar plant which have spring up since the rain this tract of country exactly resemble the stony desert describe by captain sturt as exist 200 mile to the westward these remarkable feature form the declivity of the sandstone tableland through which cooper 's creek force its way and by confine the water to a narrower space during flood cause the fine deep reach of water which characterize it 8th June by follow the western limit of the plain we reach latitude 27 degree 30 minute when the sandstone tableland recede and a boundless expanse of mud plain be before we the line of box-tree which have hitherto mark the channel nearly cease polygonum and atriplex constitute the main feature of the vegetation cooper 's creek 9th June after toiling south-west a day and a half over this level surface to latitude 27 degree 50 minute we approach some low ridge at the foot of which there be a lagoon 100 yard wide exhibit sign of a current during flood to the north-west and as there be a evident westerly trend in all the smaller channel previously cross it be evident they would soon merge in cooper 's creek steer west-north-west the several channel collect together and soon form a deep watercourse with fine reach of water the sandstone tableland close in on both side the soil of the intervene plain be much firmer but show by the vegetation that saline nature which so often attend the development of the upper sandstone in australium grass be abundant and it be surprising with what rapidity the horse recover they strength boundary of south australia 12th June approach the 141st meridian which be the boundary of the province of south australia stony ridge close in on both bank of cooper 's creek form almost a natural division across which we follow a well-beaten native path and here i observe the only instance which have come under my observation where the aborigine have take the trouble to remove natural obstacle from they path the loose stone have be clear from the track and in some place pile in large heap 14th June after pass the stony ridge the valley become wider the hill recede suddenly in longitude 140 degree 30 minute both to the north and south and the whole of the country to the west seem to consist of a succession of low ridge of red sand and level plain of dry mud subject to inundation shortly before reach the branch of cooper 's creek name by captain sturt streletzkus creek we observe the track of two horse one apparently a cart-horse and the other a well-bred animal but as none of they track be within the last month the rain have obliterate they to such a extent that they could not be trace up as they have leave the bank of the creek on the first fall of rain as be the usual habit of horse whose wanderings be uncontrolled there can be little doubt that these horse belong to captain sturt who leave one in a exhaust state near this locality and also lose a second horse whose track be follow many mile in the direction of this part of cooper 's creek 16th June streletzkus creek which separate nearly at a right angle from the main channel appear to convey about one-third of the water of cooper 's creek nearly south and as we afterwards ascertain connect it with lake torren we however continue to follow the channel which trend west for thirty mile but large branch continually break off to the south and west and at length the whole be lose on the wide plain of dry mud between the sand ridge and as there be no prospect of either water or grass to the west i steer south and south-east for fifty mile over a succession of ridge of red drift sand ten to fifty foot high run parallel to each other and in a nearly north and south direction between these ridge we occasionally find shallow puddle of rainwater or rather mud as it be so thick with clay as to be scarcely fluid fortunately a great quantity of green weed have grow up since the rain and the horse improve in condition and do not require much water 21st June to 25th June in latitude 28 degree 24 minute we again come on streletzkus creek and then follow it nearly south-south-west between sandy ridge to latitude 29 degree 25 minute when it turn to the west and enter lake torren no permanent water be see in the bed of the creek though there be many deep hollow which when once fill retain water for several month and this combine with the existence of a fine reach of water in cooper 's creek immediately above the point where streletzkus creek branch off render it far the best line of route into the interior which have yet be discover pass between the eastern point of lake torren and what have hitherto be consider the eastern arm but now ascertain to be a independent lake the space between -lrb- about half a mile -rrb- be level sandy ground cover with salicornium without any apparent connect channel the course be continue south-south-west towards mount hopeless at the northern extreme of the high range of south australium which have be visible across the level country at a distance of sixty mile 26th June as we approach the range of hill track of cattle and horse be observe and eight mile beyond mount hopeless come to a cattle station which have be lately establish by mr baker as the nature of the country we have traverse be such as not to admit of any useful deviation from it if we return to new south wale by land i deem it advisable to proceed forthwith to adelaide and dispose of the horse and equipment return with the party by sea to sydney arrive in adelaide south australia general observation 31st July we therefore proceed by easy stage towards adelaide experience the greatest hospitality at the station on we route while we reception in the city be of the most flattering nature he excellency sir richard macdonald kindly give I the use of a extensive paddock for the horse and provide quarter for the man during the period which necessarily elapse before the sale of the equipment of the expedition be effect i have also to express my acknowledgment of the kind assistance render by the honorable the commissioner of crown land to the surveyor-general and the superintendent of telegraph for valuable datum connect with the construction of the map of the route as well as to many other gentleman whose cordial co-operation greatly facilitate my arrangement it be extremely gratifying to record my appreciation of the untiring zeal and energy which distinguish every individual compose the expedition and it be to the unvarying and cheerful alacrity with which each and all perform they respective duty that under providence the rapidity and success of the journey be to be mainly attribute with reference to the probable fate of dr leichhardt it be evident from the existence of the marked camp nearly eighty mile beyond those see by mr hely that the account give to that gentleman by the native of the murder of the party be untrue and i be incline to think only a revival of the report current during leichhardt 's first journey to port essington nor be it probable that they be destroy until they have leave the victorium as if kill by the native the scatter bone of the horse and cattle would have be observe during we search i be therefore of opinion that they leave the river at the junction of the alice and favor by thunder-shower penetrate the level desert country to the north-west in which case on the cessation of the rain the party would not only be deprive of a supply of water for the onward journey but unable to retreat as the shallow character of the country traverse from the out-station on the dawson river to the head of the warrego river be generally that of a grassy forest with ridge of dense brigalow scrub a great portion be available for pastoral purpose but not well water and the soil be sandy the grass would soon be destroy if too heavily stock as we advance into the interior it become more barren and except along the bank of the larger watercourse destitute of timber and the character of the vegetation indicate excessive drought north of latitude 26 degree dense scrub of acacia prevail on the level country beyond the influence of the inundation but to the southward sandy and stony desert with low shrubby vegetation be the characteristic feature west of longitude 147 degree nearly to the boundary of south australia in 141 degree the country be unfit for occupation for though in favourable season there might in some few locality be abundance of feed for stock the uncertainty of rain and frequent recurrence of drought render it untenable the grass and herbage be principally annual which not only die but be sweep away by the hot summer wind leave the surface of the soil completely bare on cooper 's creek near the boundary there be a small tract of second-rate country which be abundantly supply with water may eventually be occupy the best part be however within the province of south australium between cooper 's creek and lake torren about 120 mile of sandy country intervene this tract be destitute of surface water but as it be probable that it could be obtain by sink well of moderate depth i think it might be occupy to advantage during the cool season and thus relieve the station which be now establish within lake torren though i fear that the summer heat would be too great to admit of permanent occupation the geological character of the country be remarkably uniform carboniferous sandstone and shale contain occasional bed of coal with superincumbent hill and ridge of basalt extend from darling downs to the 146th meridian where these rock be cover by horizontal sandstone with bed of chert and water-worn quartz pebble this latter formation extend as far as mount hopeless where the slate range of south australia rise abruptly from the plain the sandy desert and mud plain be only superficial deposit as the sandstone be often expose where the upper formation be intersect by gully the direction of the parallel ridge of drift sand appear to be the result of the prevail wind and not the action of water it be sufficient to visit they on a windy day to be convince that it be unnecessary to seek for a more remote and obscure cause than that which be in present operation it be perhaps with reference to the physical geography of australium that the result of the expedition be most important as by connect successively the exploration of sir t mitchell mr kennedy captain sturt and mr eyre the water of the tropical interior of the eastern portion of the continent be prove to flow towards spencer 's gulf if not actually into it the barometrical observation show that lake torren the lowest part of the interior be decidedly above the sea-level although only about one-third of the water of cooper 's creek flow into lake torren by the channel of streletzkus creek there be strong evidence that the remain channel after spread they water on the vast plain which occupy the country between they and sturt 's stony desert finally drain to the south augmented probably by the water of eyre 's creek the stony desert and perhaps some other watercourse of a similar character come from the westward this peculiar structure of the interior render it improbable that any considerable inland lake should exist in connection with the known system of water for as lake torren be decidedly only a expand continuation of cooper 's creek and therefore the culminate point of this vast system of drainage if there be sufficient average fall of rain in the interior to balance the effect of evaporation from the surface of a extensive sheet of water the torren basin instead of be occupy by salt marsh in which the existence of anything beyond shallow lagoon of salt-water be yet problematical would be maintain as a permanent lake therefore if the water flow from so large a tract of country be insufficient to meet the evaporation from the surface of lake torren there be even less probability of the water of the western interior form a inland lake of any magnitude even should there be so anomalous a feature as a depression of the surface in which it could be collect especially as we knowledge of its limit indicate a much drier climate and less favourable conformation of surface than in the eastern division of the continent the undulation of the surface of the country be nearly parallel to the meridian gradually decrease in height from the divide range between the eastern and western water till instead of the water of the river be confine to valley they occupy plain form by a slight flattening of the curvature of the sphere thus the side of the plain through which the river run before it turn west to cooper 's creek be 150 foot below the tangential level of the center channel and even the summit of the sandstone tableland which rise beyond be below the visible horizon it be this peculiar conformation which cause the stream-bed to spread so widely when follow the course of the valley from north to south and it be only where they break through the intervene ridge that the water be confine sufficiently to form well-defined channel the existence of these extensive valley trend north and south over so large a tract of country render it by no means unlikely that they continue far beyond the limit of present exploration and it be not unreasonable to infer that the great depression which have be trace nearly five hundred mile north from spencer 's gulf through lake torren to the stony desert of sturt -lrb- or rather the mud plain contiguous to its western limit -rrb- may be continuous for a equal distance beyond to the low land at the head of the gulf of carpentarium a theory also support by the fact that the river flow into the gulf either come from the east or west apparently from higher land in those direction while there be not a single watercourse from the south or any indication of elevated country in that direction captain wickham have name a important river discover by he in hm beagle on the north-west coast the victorium several year prior to sir t mitchell have attach that name to the upper portion of cooper 's creek which have also be previously discover and name by captain sturt i would suggest that the term river cooper be adopt for the whole of the main channel from its source discover by sir t mitchell to its termination in lake torren as while it do not interfere with the rule that the name give by the first discoverer should be retain will prevent the recurrence of the misapprehension and inconvenience of have two important river with the same designation on the map of australium with regard to the number and habit of the aborigine i could collect little information as only a collective number of about 100 man a few woman and child be see in small scatter party but judge from the number of encampment see at least a thousand must visit the bank of the river and it be probable that the whole of the inhabitant for at least 100 mile on each side be dependent on it for water during the dry season neither sex wear any clothing they weapon and utensil be similar to those use on the eastern coast nor be there any characteristic by which they could be observe to differ from the aborigine of other portion of australium fish rat grass seed and a few root constitute they chief food on the upper part of the river they bury they dead pile wood on the grave near the junction of the thompson they suspend the body in net and afterwards remove the bone while on cooper 's creek the grave be mound of earth three to four foot high apparently without any excavation and surmount by a pile of dead wood in the last-named locality the number of burial mound which have be construct about two year ago greatly exceed the proportion of death which could have possibly occur in any ordinary season of mortality even assume the densest population know in any other part of australium and it be not improbable that the season of drought which prove so destructive to the tree vegetation higher up the river may have be equally disastrous in its effect on the aboriginal
